- Chain searches logically: search → read → references → definition
- Don't re-search for the same pattern; use results from prior calls

# Architecture Document: Envoy HTTP Connection Manager

**Repository:** github.com/sg-evals/envoy--1d0ba73a (mirror of envoyproxy/envoy)
**Output:** Write your document to `/workspace/documentation.md`

## Task

Produce an architecture document for Envoy's **HTTP Connection Manager** (HCM) subsystem. The document must explain how the major components interact to process an HTTP request from arrival on a downstream connection through to upstream dispatch. Do not simply list APIs — explain the **design**, **data flow**, and **extension points**.

## Scope

Your document must cover these four components and how they work together:

### 1. ConnectionManagerImpl
The central network filter that owns the connection lifecycle. Explain:
- How it implements `Network::ReadFilter` to receive raw bytes
- How it creates and manages `ActiveStream` objects for each HTTP request
- Its role in codec creation (lazy codec instantiation for H1/H2 vs. H3)
- Connection-level concerns: drain decisions, overload management, watermark-based flow control

### 2. FilterManager and the HTTP Filter Chain
The per-stream filter chain execution engine. Explain:
- The decoder filter chain (request path) and encoder filter chain (response path)
- How `FilterChainFactory` creates filters for each stream
- Filter iteration: how `decodeHeaders`/`decodeData`/`decodeTrailers` propagate through decoder filters
- How filters can stop iteration, modify headers, or send local replies
- The distinction between `StreamDecoderFilter`, `StreamEncoderFilter`, and `StreamFilter` (dual)

### 3. Router Filter
The terminal decoder filter that forwards requests upstream. Explain:
- Route selection: how the router uses `RouteConfiguration` to pick a cluster
- How it obtains an HTTP connection pool from `ClusterManager`
- Upstream request lifecycle: `UpstreamRequest` creation, retry logic, timeout handling
- Shadow routing and hedged request support (if applicable)

### 4. Cluster Manager and Upstream Connectivity
The upstream connection pool and cluster management layer. Explain:
- How `ClusterManagerImpl` provides connection pools per cluster
- Load balancing: how the router obtains a host from the cluster's load balancer
- Connection pool mechanics: the relationship between logical connection pools and physical connections
- How health checking and outlier detection feed back into the load balancer

## Document Requirements

1. **Component Responsibilities** — what each component owns
2. **Data Flow** — the path of an HTTP request from downstream bytes to upstream dispatch, and the response path back
3. **Extension Points** — where users extend Envoy (HTTP filters, cluster extensions, load balancers, access loggers)
4. **Error Handling** — how errors at each stage (codec errors, filter errors, upstream failures) are handled
5. **relevant source files** — reference the actual source files in the envoyproxy/envoy repository

## Anti-Requirements

- Do NOT generate a simple API listing or header-file dump
- Do NOT fabricate class names or file paths that don't exist in the repository
- Do NOT cover Envoy components outside the HCM request path (e.g., xDS config delivery, listener management)

     1→# Envoy HTTP Connection Manager Architecture
     2→
     3→## Overview
     4→
     5→The HTTP Connection Manager (HCM) is Envoy's core subsystem for processing HTTP requests from downstream clients through to upstream servers. It acts as a **network-level filter** that owns the full lifecycle of downstream TCP/QUIC connections, creating and managing per-stream HTTP processing pipelines.
     6→
     7→The HCM architecture centers on four primary components working together:
     8→
     9→1. **ConnectionManagerImpl** — Connection lifecycle manager and codec orchestrator
    10→2. **FilterManager and HTTP Filter Chain** — Per-stream request/response processing engine
    11→3. **Router Filter** — Terminal decoder filter that performs route selection and upstream dispatch
    12→4. **Cluster Manager and Upstream Connectivity** — Upstream connection pooling and load balancing
    13→
    14→### Key Design Principles
    15→
    16→- **Protocol Abstraction**: Codecs (HTTP/1.1, HTTP/2, HTTP/3) are abstracted behind a common interface, allowing HCM to process streams uniformly regardless of protocol.
    17→- **Lazy Codec Instantiation**: Codecs are created on-demand (H1/H2 on first `onData()`, H3 on `onNewConnection()`), avoiding unnecessary overhead for idle connections.
    18→- **Streaming Request/Response Processing**: The filter chain processes data as it arrives via callbacks (`decodeHeaders`, `decodeData`, `decodeTrailers`), enabling low-latency proxying.
    19→- **Filter Chain Iteration Control**: Filters can pause iteration, buffer data, or abort processing, allowing sophisticated request/response manipulation without blocking the event loop.
    20→
    21→---
    22→
    23→## Component Responsibilities
    24→
    25→### 1. ConnectionManagerImpl
    26→
... (truncated)

## Document Summary

### 📋 **Structure**

1. **Overview** — High-level introduction to the HCM subsystem and its four core components
2. **Key Design Principles** — Explanations of protocol abstraction, lazy codec instantiation, streaming processing, and filter iteration control
3. **Component Responsibilities** — Deep dive into each of the four components:
   - **ConnectionManagerImpl**: Connection/codec lifecycle, stream creation, overload management
   - **FilterManager & HTTP Filter Chain**: Decoder/encoder chain execution, iteration control, local reply generation
   - **Router Filter**: Route selection, upstream host selection, retry logic, shadow routing
   - **Cluster Manager**: Load balancing, connection pooling, thread-local state management
4. **Data Flow** — Detailed request path (downstream to upstream), response path, and stream completion flows with ASCII diagrams

   - HTTP Filters (custom authentication, transformation, etc.)

   - Access Logging
   - Request ID Generation
   - Custom Filter State
   - Tracing integration

   - Codec errors

  "content": "# Envoy HTTP Connection Manager Architecture\n\n## Overview\n\nThe HTTP Connection Manager (HCM) is Envoy's core subsystem for processing HTTP requests from downstream clients through to upstream servers. It acts as a **network-level filter** that owns the full lifecycle of downstream TCP/QUIC connections, creating and managing per-stream HTTP processing pipelines.\n\nThe HCM architecture centers on four primary components working together:\n\n1. **ConnectionManagerImpl** \u2014 Connection lifecycle manager and codec orchestrator\n2. **FilterManager and HTTP Filter Chain** \u2014 Per-stream request/response processing engine\n3. **Router Filter** \u2014 Terminal decoder filter that performs route selection and upstream dispatch\n4. **Cluster Manager and Upstream Connectivity** \u2014 Upstream connection pooling and load balancing\n\n### Key Design Principles\n\n- **Protocol Abstraction**: Codecs (HTTP/1.1, HTTP/2, HTTP/3) are abstracted behind a common interface, allowing HCM to process streams uniformly regardless of protocol.\n- **Lazy Codec Instantiation**: Codecs are created on-demand (H1/H2 on first `onData()`, H3 on `onNewConnection()`), avoiding unnecessary overhead for idle connections.\n- **Streaming Request/Response Processing**: The filter chain processes data as it arrives via callbacks (`decodeHeaders`, `decodeData`, `decodeTrailers`), enabling low-latency proxying.\n- **Filter Chain Iteration Control**: Filters can pause iteration, buffer data, or abort processing, allowing sophisticated request/response manipulation without blocking the event loop.\n\n---\n\n## Component Responsibilities\n\n### 1. ConnectionManagerImpl\n\n**File**: `source/common/http/conn_manager_impl.h/cc`\n\nConnectionManagerImpl is the central bridge between the network layer and HTTP processing. It implements `Network::ReadFilter` and acts as both a connection-level manager and a stream factory.\n\n#### Responsibilities:\n\n**Connection Lifecycle Management**:\n- Implements `Network::ReadFilter::onData()` to receive raw TCP/QUIC bytes\n- Manages connection-level state: idle timelines, max duration, drain decisions\n- Tracks active streams in a doubly-linked list (`streams_`)\n- Signals connection events (close, reset, watermark changes) to all active streams\n\n**Codec Creation and Ownership**:\n- Lazily creates the codec on first `onData()` call (H1/H2) or `onConnection()` (H3)\n- Selects codec based on `codec_type` config or ALPN negotiation\n- Routes incoming data to the codec for stream demultiplexing\n- Handles codec events (stream creation via `newStream()`, protocol errors)\n\n**Stream Lifecycle**:\n- Implements `ServerConnectionCallbacks::newStream()` to create `ActiveStream` objects when the codec receives a new HTTP stream\n- Tracks stream completion and schedules deferred deletion\n- Manages stream-level cleanup: timers, filters, logging\n- Enforces per-connection limits: max requests, request header size, idle timeouts\n\n**Overload and Flow Control**:\n- Integrates with the overload manager to check load shedding points (e.g., `HcmDecodeHeaders`)\n- Manages connection-level write buffer watermarks via `onAboveWriteBufferHighWatermark()` / `onBelowWriteBufferLowWatermark()`\n- Propagates watermark events to the codec and all streams\n\n**Drain State Management**:\n- Decides when to drain connections (max requests reached, graceful shutdown, premature resets detected)\n- Coordinates drain state transitions and sends GOAWAY frames for HTTP/2\n\n**Key State**:\n```cpp\nServerConnectionPtr codec_;        // Protocol codec (H1, H2, or H3)\nstd::list<LinkedObject<ActiveStream>> streams_;  // Active HTTP streams\nDrainState drain_state_;           // Connection drain status\nuint32_t accumulated_requests_;    // Requests processed on this connection\n```\n\n#### Entry Points:\n\n- **`onData(Buffer::Instance&, bool end_stream)`**: Network filter receives downstream bytes \u2192 forwards to codec\n- **`newStream(ResponseEncoder&, bool)`**: Codec signals new HTTP stream \u2192 creates `ActiveStream` and filter chain\n\n---\n\n### 2. FilterManager and HTTP Filter Chain\n\n**Files**: `source/common/http/filter_manager.h/cc`\n\nThe FilterManager is a per-stream filter chain execution engine. It orchestrates the execution of both decoder filters (request path) and encoder filters (response path), managing iteration state, buffering, and local reply generation.\n\n#### Responsibilities:\n\n**Request Processing (Decoder Chain)**:\n- Iterates through decoder filters in order for `decodeHeaders()`, `decodeData()`, `decodeTrailers()`, and `decodeMetadata()`\n- Maintains a `StreamDecoderFilters` collection for forward iteration\n- Stops iteration if a filter returns `StopIteration` or `StopAllIteration`\n- Buffers data if iteration is paused, respecting the stream's buffer limit\n- Calls `onDestroy()` on all filters when the stream completes\n\n**Response Processing (Encoder Chain)**:\n- Iterates through encoder filters in **reverse order** (last filter first)\n- Maintains a `StreamEncoderFilters` collection with reverse iteration\n- Mirrors decoder chain semantics: iteration control, buffering, pause handling\n- Flushes any buffered data when iteration resumes\n\n**Local Reply Generation**:\n- Supports sending local replies (e.g., 404, timeout, authentication failure) without forwarding upstream\n- Can be triggered by filters or HCM (via `FilterManager::sendLocalReply()`)\n- Prepares local replies through all encoder filters to allow header manipulation\n- Properly terminates the decoder chain so no further request processing occurs\n\n**Iteration State Management**:\n- Tracks decode/encode state for each filter: `IterationState::Continue`, `StopIteration`, `StopAllBuffer`, `StopAllWatermark`\n- Buffers data separately if stopped for backpressure (`StopAllWatermark`) vs. custom logic (`StopAllBuffer`)\n- Resumes iteration when a paused filter calls `continueIteration()`\n\n**Watermark and Flow Control**:\n- Manages high/low watermark callbacks for backpressure\n- Calls `onAboveWriteBufferHighWatermark()` / `onBelowWriteBufferLowWatermark()` on subscribed filters\n- Tracks buffered data size and enforces per-stream buffer limits\n\n**Key Abstractions**:\n\n- **`StreamDecoderFilter`**: Implements `decodeHeaders()`, `decodeData()`, `decodeTrailers()`, `decodeMetadata()`\n- **`StreamEncoderFilter`**: Implements `encodeHeaders()`, `encodeData()`, `encodeTrailers()`, `encodeMetadata()`\n- **`StreamFilter`**: Dual filter implementing both decoder and encoder interfaces (e.g., Router filter is a `StreamDecoderFilter`)\n- **`StreamDecoderFilterCallbacks`**: Callbacks for filters to interact with the stream (e.g., `streamInfo()`, `sendLocalReply()`)\n\n#### Filter Chain Creation:\n\nThe FilterManager uses a `FilterChainFactory` (injected at HCM config time) to instantiate filters for each stream:\n\n1. HCM calls `config_->filterFactory().createFilterChain(callbacks)` at stream creation\n2. The factory iterates through configured HTTP filters and instantiates each via a filter config provider\n3. Filters are added to the decoder/encoder chains in registration order\n4. The chain is immutable after creation\n\n#### Key State:\n\n```cpp\nstruct StreamDecoderFilters { std::vector<ActiveStreamDecoderFilterPtr> entries_; };\nstruct StreamEncoderFilters { std::vector<ActiveStreamEncoderFilterPtr> entries_; };\nBuffer::InstancePtr buffered_request_data_;   // Buffered during decoder pause\nBuffer::InstancePtr buffered_response_data_;  // Buffered during encoder pause\nuint64_t buffer_limit_;                       // Max bytes to buffer per stream\n```\n\n---\n\n### 3. Router Filter\n\n**Files**: `source/common/router/router.h/cc`\n\nThe Router filter is the terminal decoder filter in the standard HTTP filter chain. Its primary role is route selection and upstream request forwarding.\n\n#### Responsibilities:\n\n**Route Selection**:\n- Implements `Http::StreamDecoderFilter::decodeHeaders()` to select a route from the configured `RouteConfiguration`\n- Uses `downstreamHeaders()`, stream metadata, and connection context to match against route matchers\n- Selects a cluster name from the matched route's action\n- Caches the selected route in `StreamInfo` for downstream filters and access logs\n\n**Upstream Host Selection**:\n- Queries the cluster manager for a `ThreadLocalCluster` using the route's cluster name\n- Calls the cluster's load balancer to select a specific `Host` endpoint\n- Respects load balancer context from request metadata, cookies, or header-based hash policies\n- Handles load balancer cancellation if host selection takes time or times out\n\n**Upstream Connection Pool Acquisition**:\n- Obtains an HTTP connection pool from the cluster manager for the selected host\n- Passes protocol selection, connection options, and transport socket options\n- Creates a `GenericConnPool` abstraction that works with both HTTP and TCP upstreams\n\n**UpstreamRequest Lifecycle**:\n- Creates an `UpstreamRequest` object for each request to be sent upstream\n- Passes request headers via `acceptHeadersFromRouter()`\n- Passes request data via `acceptDataFromRouter()`\n- Receives upstream response via callbacks on `RouterFilterInterface`\n\n**Retry and Timeout Logic**:\n- Sets up per-try timeouts and global request timeouts\n- Detects retryable upstream failures (connection refused, 503, etc.)\n- Implements exponential backoff and max retry limits\n- Handles hedged requests: spawning parallel upstream requests if `per_try_timeout` is exceeded\n\n**Shadow Routing** (optional):\n- Can spawn shadow requests to a different cluster for testing/canary purposes\n- Shadow requests do not impact the primary response\n- Configured via `RouteEntry::shadowPolicy()`\n\n**Key State**:\n\n```cpp\nstd::list<UpstreamRequestPtr> upstream_requests_;  // Active upstream requests (main + retries + hedges)\nRouter::RouteConstSharedPtr route_;                // Selected route\nUpstream::ClusterInfoConstSharedPtr cluster_;      // Selected cluster\nstd::vector<UpstreamRequest*> pending_hedge_requests_;  // Hedged requests awaiting timeout\n```\n\n#### Filter Interface:\n\n- **`decodeHeaders(RequestHeaderMap&, bool)`**: Select route, host, and create first upstream request\n- **`decodeData(Buffer::Instance&, bool)`**: Forward data to all active upstream requests\n- **`decodeTrailers(RequestTrailerMap&)`**: Forward trailers to upstream\n- **`decodeMetadata(MetadataMap&)`**: Forward metadata to upstream\n- **`onUpstreamHeaders(uint64_t, ResponseHeaderMapPtr&&, UpstreamRequest&, bool)`**: Receive upstream response headers\n- **`onUpstreamData(Buffer::Instance&, UpstreamRequest&, bool)`**: Receive upstream response body\n- **`onUpstreamTrailers(ResponseTrailerMapPtr&&, UpstreamRequest&)`**: Receive upstream response trailers\n\n---\n\n### 4. Cluster Manager and Upstream Connectivity\n\n**Files**: `source/common/upstream/cluster_manager_impl.h/cc`\n\nThe Cluster Manager is Envoy's centralized manager for upstream clusters. It abstracts away cluster membership updates, load balancing, and connection pooling.\n\n#### Responsibilities:\n\n**Cluster Management**:\n- Maintains dynamic cluster configurations via xDS (Cluster Discovery Service)\n- Provides thread-local views of clusters for efficient access without synchronization\n- Implements cluster health checks and outlier detection\n- Notifies listeners of cluster updates (used for graceful connection draining)\n\n**Load Balancer Integration**:\n- Each cluster owns a load balancer (Round Robin, Least Request, Maglev, Random, etc.)\n- The load balancer is queried to select a specific `Host` from the cluster's membership\n- Accepts `LoadBalancerContext` from the router filter containing request metadata, cookies, and headers\n- Implements deterministic selection via consistent hashing and metadata matching\n\n**Connection Pool Management**:\n- Maintains per-host, per-priority, per-protocol connection pools\n- Allocates new pools on-demand and reuses them across requests\n- Manages physical TCP/QUIC connection lifecycle: creation, reuse, closing\n- Implements connection idle detection and draining\n\n**Thread-Local Cluster State**:\n- Stores cluster state in thread-local storage to avoid locks\n- Each worker thread maintains its own set of connection pools\n- Periodically (e.g., on cluster updates) primes thread-local state via callbacks\n\n#### Connection Pool Mechanics:\n\nA connection pool represents a set of physical connections to a single upstream host:\n\n1. **Pool Request**: Router calls `cluster->httpConnPool(host, priority, protocol)` \u2192 returns pool\n2. **Stream Creation**: Router calls `pool->newStream(callbacks)` \u2192 pool either returns existing connection or creates new one\n3. **Connection Ready**: Pool invokes `callbacks->onPoolReady(upstream, ...)` \u2192 UpstreamRequest begins sending data\n4. **Connection Failure**: Pool invokes `callbacks->onPoolFailure(reason)` \u2192 router triggers retry logic\n\n#### Key Abstractions:\n\n- **`Cluster`**: Represents a named group of upstream endpoints; owns load balancer and config\n- **`Host`**: An individual upstream endpoint with address, health status, and metadata\n- **`ClusterManager`**: Factory for getting thread-local views of clusters\n- **`ThreadLocalCluster`**: Per-worker-thread view; provides `chooseHost()` and `httpConnPool()`\n- **`ConnectionPool::Instance`**: Manages connections to a single host; spawns new streams on available connections\n\n#### Load Balancing:\n\n1. Router calls `cluster->loadBalancer()->chooseHost(context)` to select a host\n2. Load balancer uses context's hash key, metadata, or direct host assignment\n3. Returns a host or nullptr if all hosts are unhealthy\n4. Router then queries the connection pool for that host\n\n---\n\n## Data Flow\n\n### Request Path (Downstream to Upstream)\n\n```\nDownstream TCP/QUIC bytes\n    \u2193\nConnectionManagerImpl::onData()\n    \u2193\n[Create codec if needed (H1/H2 on first data, H3 on connection)]\n    \u2193\nCodec demultiplexes stream from bytes\n    \u2193\nCodec::ServerConnectionCallbacks::newStream(response_encoder, stream_id)\n    \u2193\nConnectionManagerImpl::newStream()\n    \u251c\u2500 Create ActiveStream\n    \u251c\u2500 Create buffer account for watermark tracking\n    \u251c\u2500 Create FilterManager\n    \u251c\u2500 Call filterFactory_.createFilterChain(callbacks)\n    \u2502   \u2514\u2500 Instantiate all configured HTTP filters\n    \u2514\u2500 Return RequestDecoder to codec\n    \u2193\nCodec calls RequestDecoder::decodeHeaders(headers, end_stream)\n    \u2193\nConnectionManagerImpl::ActiveStream::decodeHeaders()\n    \u251c\u2500 Pass headers to FilterManager\n    \u2514\u2500 FilterManager::decodeHeaders(headers, end_stream)\n        \u251c\u2500 Iterate decoder filters in order\n        \u251c\u2500 Call filter1->decodeHeaders(), filter2->decodeHeaders(), ..., routerFilter->decodeHeaders()\n        \u251c\u2500 Router filter selects route and creates upstream request(s)\n        \u2514\u2500 Each filter returns FilterHeadersStatus:\n           - Continue \u2192 next filter\n           - StopIteration \u2192 buffer data, wait for continueIteration()\n           - StopAllIteration \u2192 buffer all data, don't call further filters\n    \u2193\n[Router filter creates UpstreamRequest and acquires connection pool]\n    \u2193\nUpstreamRequest::acceptHeadersFromRouter(end_stream)\n    \u251c\u2500 Pass headers to UpstreamFilterManager\n    \u2514\u2500 Iterate upstream HTTP filters (if configured)\n        \u2514\u2500 Call codec filter to encode headers\n    \u2193\n[Upstream connection established or reused from pool]\n    \u2193\nCodec::newStream() \u2192 RequestEncoder\n    \u2193\nRequestEncoder encodes request headers to upstream connection\n    \u2193\nCodec calls RequestDecoder::decodeData(data, end_stream) [if body present]\n    \u2193\nConnectionManagerImpl::ActiveStream::decodeData()\n    \u2514\u2500 FilterManager::decodeData(data, end_stream)\n        \u2514\u2500 Iterate decoder filters, forward data to router\n    \u2193\nUpstreamRequest::acceptDataFromRouter(data, end_stream)\n    \u2514\u2500 Iterate upstream filters, encode to RequestEncoder\n    \u2193\nRequestEncoder writes data to upstream connection buffer\n    \u2193\n[Repeat for trailers and metadata if present]\n```\n\n### Response Path (Upstream to Downstream)\n\n```\nUpstream bytes arrive on connection\n    \u2193\nCodec decodes upstream response\n    \u2193\nResponseDecoder callbacks fired (e.g., decodeHeaders, decodeData, decodeTrailers)\n    \u2193\nUpstreamRequest::decodeHeaders(headers, end_stream) [response headers]\n    \u251c\u2500 Pass headers through UpstreamFilterManager (filters in reverse order)\n    \u2514\u2500 Call RouterFilterInterface::onUpstreamHeaders(status, headers, upstream_request, end_stream)\n    \u2193\nRouter::onUpstreamHeaders()\n    \u251c\u2500 Store response headers in stream\n    \u2514\u2500 Call FilterManager::encodeHeaders(headers, end_stream)\n        \u251c\u2500 Iterate encoder filters in reverse order\n        \u251c\u2500 Call routerFilter->encodeHeaders(), filter2->encodeHeaders(), ..., filter1->encodeHeaders()\n        \u2514\u2500 Each filter returns FilterHeadersStatus:\n           - Continue \u2192 next filter\n           - StopIteration \u2192 buffer data, wait for continueIteration()\n    \u2193\n[Encoder filters can modify response headers (add authentication, rewrite location, etc.)]\n    \u2193\nLast encoder filter (or early encoder if no filters) calls ResponseEncoder::encodeHeaders()\n    \u2193\nDownstream codec encodes headers to client connection\n    \u2193\n[Response body and trailers follow same path through encoder filters]\n    \u2193\nBytes sent to downstream client\n```\n\n### Stream Completion\n\n```\nEither upstream sends end_stream or decoder filter aborts:\n    \u2193\nFilterManager::maybeEndDecode(terminal_filter_end_stream)\n    \u251c\u2500 Marks decoder chain as complete\n    \u251c\u2500 Stops accepting further request data\n    \u2514\u2500 If encoder already complete \u2192 checkAndCloseStream()\n    \u2193\nFilterManager::maybeEndEncode(end_stream)\n    \u251c\u2500 Marks encoder chain as complete\n    \u251c\u2500 Stops accepting further response data\n    \u2514\u2500 If decoder already complete \u2192 checkAndCloseStream()\n    \u2193\nFilterManager::checkAndCloseStream()\n    \u251c\u2500 Call filter->onStreamComplete() for all filters\n    \u251c\u2500 Destroy filters\n    \u2514\u2500 Return stream to ConnectionManagerImpl\n    \u2193\nConnectionManagerImpl::doDeferredStreamDestroy()\n    \u251c\u2500 Log access logs\n    \u251c\u2500 Disable timers\n    \u251c\u2500 Reset stream if needed (e.g., for protocol errors)\n    \u2514\u2500 Schedule stream deletion via dispatcher.deferredDelete()\n    \u2193\nStream memory freed; connection ready for next stream\n```\n\n---\n\n## Extension Points\n\nEnvoy's HTTP request processing is highly extensible through several well-defined extension mechanisms:\n\n### 1. HTTP Filters\n\n**Interface**: `StreamDecoderFilter`, `StreamEncoderFilter`, `StreamFilter`\n\nHTTP filters are the primary extension point. Custom filters can:\n- Inspect and modify request/response headers, body, trailers\n- Implement authentication, authorization, rate limiting, load shedding\n- Perform request/response body transformation (compression, encryption)\n- Generate local replies (short-circuit requests)\n- Control filter iteration (pause, resume, abort)\n\n**Example**: The built-in router filter is itself an HTTP filter implementing `StreamDecoderFilter`.\n\n**Registration**: Filters are registered in the HTTP connection manager config:\n```yaml\nhttp_filters:\n  - name: envoy.filters.http.auth\n    typed_config: { ... }\n  - name: envoy.filters.http.lua\n    typed_config: { ... }\n  - name: envoy.filters.http.router  # Always last\n    typed_config: { ... }\n```\n\nFilters are instantiated via a `FilterChainFactory` that is passed to each `FilterManager`.\n\n### 2. Route Configuration and Cluster Selection\n\n**Interface**: `RouteConfiguration`, `RouteEntry`, `Route`\n\nRoutes define how requests are matched and forwarded:\n- **Matchers**: Path prefix/exact/regex, headers, methods, query parameters\n- **Actions**: Forward to cluster, redirect, direct response, circuit breaking rules\n- **Request Transformation**: Add/remove headers, request ID generation\n- **Retry Policy**: Max retries, retryable status codes, backoff strategy\n- **Timeout**: Request timeout, per-try timeout\n- **Mirror/Shadow**: Route a copy of the request to another cluster\n\nRoutes can be:\n- Statically configured in the bootstrap config\n- Dynamically updated via RDS (Route Discovery Service)\n- Scoped to specific criteria (virtual hosts, per-node configuration)\n\n### 3. Load Balancing\n\n**Interface**: `LoadBalancer`, `LoadBalancerContext`\n\nCluster managers use pluggable load balancers:\n- **Round Robin**: Distribute evenly across healthy hosts\n- **Least Request**: Route to host with fewest active requests\n- **Maglev**: Consistent hashing with deterministic subset selection\n- **Random**: Random host selection\n- **Original Destination**: Route to upstream's original destination IP\n\nCustom load balancers can implement sophisticated algorithms (e.g., per-cookie session affinity, ML-based routing).\n\nLoad balancers receive `LoadBalancerContext` from the router:\n```cpp\nstruct LoadBalancerContext {\n  absl::optional<uint64_t> hash_key;           // Consistent hash\n  const Protobuf::Struct* connection_metadata; // Dynamic metadata\n  const Protobuf::Struct* request_metadata;    // Request-specific metadata\n};\n```\n\n### 4. Upstream Connection Pools\n\n**Interface**: `ConnectionPool::InstancePtr`\n\nConnection pool factories are provided by cluster managers, allowing:\n- Custom connection pooling strategies (connection limits, idle detection)\n- Protocol negotiation (ALPN for HTTP/1.1 vs. HTTP/2)\n- Connection reuse policies (keep-alive, max requests per connection)\n\n### 5. Access Logging\n\n**Interface**: `AccessLog::InstanceSharedPtr`\n\nAccess loggers receive complete `StreamInfo` containing:\n- Request/response headers, trailers\n- Upstream cluster and host\n- Duration and timing information\n- Response flags (error conditions, retry counts)\n- Custom filter state\n\nLoggers can format and emit logs to:\n- Local file (gRPC, JSON, plaintext)\n- Remote syslog server\n- gRPC service\n- Custom backend via extension\n\n### 6. Request ID Generation\n\n**Interface**: `RequestIDExtension`\n\nCustom request ID generators can:\n- Generate request IDs based on request properties\n- Set request IDs in custom headers\n- Trace requests across distributed systems\n\n### 7. Custom Filter State\n\n**Interface**: `StreamInfo::FilterState`\n\nFilters can store arbitrary per-request or per-connection state:\n```cpp\nstream_info.filterState()->setData<MyCustomObject>(\n    \"my.custom.key\",\n    std::make_unique<MyCustomObject>(),\n    StreamInfo::FilterState::StateType::Mutable\n);\n```\n\nDownstream filters can retrieve this state and act on it.\n\n### 8. Tracing\n\n**Interface**: `Tracer`, `Span`\n\nTracers integrate with Envoy's request processing:\n- Receive span creation callbacks at critical points\n- Inject trace context into upstream request headers (via `x-b3-trace-id`, `traceparent`, etc.)\n- Extract trace context from downstream headers\n- Report spans to tracing backends (Jaeger, Zipkin, Datadog, AWS X-Ray)\n\n### 9. Stats and Metrics\n\n**Interface**: `Stats::Scope`, `Stats::Statistic`\n\nFilters and cluster managers emit rich metrics:\n- Request counts, errors, latencies\n- Upstream health status and failover events\n- Connection pooling statistics\n- Custom filter-specific metrics\n\n---\n\n## Error Handling\n\nEnvoy handles errors at multiple layers with graceful degradation:\n\n### Codec Errors (H1, H2, H3)\n\n**Detection**: Codec detects malformed headers, invalid frames, protocol violations\n\n**Handling**:\n- Codec sets `StreamInfo::DownstreamProtocolError` flag\n- Sends HTTP 400 Bad Request to client (if stream is viable)\n- If protocol is unrecoverable: closes connection with GOAWAY (H2) or connection reset (H1)\n- Logs error for debugging\n\n**Example**: Invalid HTTP/2 frame size \u2192 codec error \u2192 400 response \u2192 connection reused if possible\n\n### Filter Errors\n\n**Detection**: Filter calls `sendLocalReply()` or logs an error; filter returns `StopIteration`\n\n**Handling**:\n- FilterManager stops decoder chain execution\n- FilterManager calls `sendLocalReply()` to generate HTTP response\n- Response headers pass through remaining encoder filters\n- Stream completes normally with error response\n\n**Example**: Authentication filter denies request \u2192 `sendLocalReply(401)` \u2192 401 returned to client\n\n### Upstream Connection Failures\n\n**Detection**: Connection pool fails to connect, connection drops, or TLS handshake fails\n\n**Handling**:\n1. Pool invokes `GenericConnectionPoolCallbacks::onPoolFailure(PoolFailureReason, host)`\n2. UpstreamRequest invokes `RouterFilterInterface::onUpstreamReset(StreamResetReason)`\n3. Router checks route's retry policy:\n   - If retryable and retries remaining: create new UpstreamRequest\n   - If non-retryable or retries exhausted: send upstream error response (503, 504, etc.)\n4. Response flows back through encoder filters\n5. Stream completes with error response\n\n**Retry Backoff**: Router implements exponential backoff (jitter optional) between retries\n\n**Response Flags**: Router sets response flags in `StreamInfo` (e.g., `UpstreamConnectionFailure`, `UpstreamRequestTimeout`)\n\n### Timeout Errors\n\n**Request Timeout** (global deadline for entire request):\n- Triggered by timer if request exceeds `timeout` configured on route\n- FilterManager calls `sendLocalReply(504 Gateway Timeout)`\n- Router cancels any pending upstream requests\n\n**Per-Try Timeout** (deadline for each retry attempt):\n- Triggered by timer if individual try exceeds `per_try_timeout`\n- Router triggers retry if retries remaining\n- Enables hedged requests: if timeout expires before response, spawn parallel request\n\n**Idle Timeout** (connection-level):\n- ConnectionManagerImpl closes idle connections after `idle_timeout`\n- Prevents connection leaks if clients are hung\n\n### Upstream Protocol Errors\n\n**Detection**: Upstream sends invalid response headers, body framing errors, etc.\n\n**Handling**:\n- ResponseDecoder sets `StreamInfo::UpstreamProtocolError` flag\n- If possible, stream continues with best-effort parsing\n- Otherwise, router triggers reset and sends error response\n\n### Resource Exhaustion\n\n**High Watermark** (downstream buffer full):\n- FilterManager detects buffered data exceeds limit\n- Calls `onAboveWriteBufferHighWatermark()` on watermark subscribers (typically router)\n- Router stops reading from downstream connection (backpressure)\n- Once buffer drained: `onBelowWriteBufferLowWatermark()` resumes reading\n\n**Overload Shedding**:\n- ConnectionManagerImpl checks overload points before accepting new streams\n- If overload shed point is active: sends 503 Service Unavailable without filter processing\n- Prevents cascading failures during sustained overload\n\n---\n\n## Relevant Source Files\n\n### Core Components\n\n| Component | Header | `source/common/router/upstream_request.h` | `source/common/router/upstream_request.cc` |\n| **Cluster Manager** | `source/common/upstream/cluster_manager_impl.h` | Connection Manager is a sophisticated, modular system that processes HTTP requests through a layered pipeline:\n\n1. **Downstream Connection** \u2192 **ConnectionManagerImpl** \u2192 Codec instantiation\n2. **Per-stream Processing** \u2192 **FilterManager** \u2192 Ordered filter chain iteration\n3. **Route Selection & Forwarding** \u2192 **Router Filter** \u2192 Upstream acquisition\n4. **Upstream Connectivity** \u2192 **Cluster Manager** \u2192 Load balancing and pooling\n5. **Response Path** \u2192 Same filters in reverse \u2192 **Downstream Client**\n\nThe design is extensible through HTTP filters, custom load balancers, route configurations, and access loggers. Errors are handled gracefully with retry logic, timeouts, overload shedding, and detailed response flags for observability.\n\nThis architecture allows Envoy to efficiently process millions of requests per second while maintaining flexibility for complex request routing, transformation, and security policies.\n",

{
  "content": "# Envoy HTTP Connection Manager Architecture\n\n## Overview\n\nThe HTTP Connection Manager (HCM) is Envoy's core subsystem for processing HTTP requests from downstream clients through to upstream servers. It acts as a **network-level filter** that owns the full lifecycle of downstream TCP/QUIC connections, creating and managing per-stream HTTP processing pipelines.\n\nThe HCM architecture centers on four primary components working together:\n\n1. **ConnectionManagerImpl** \u2014 Connection lifecycle manager and codec orchestrator\n2. **FilterManager and HTTP Filter Chain** \u2014 Per-stream request/response processing engine\n3. **Router Filter** \u2014 Terminal decoder filter that performs route selection and upstream dispatch\n4. **Cluster Manager and Upstream Connectivity** \u2014 Upstream connection pooling and load balancing\n\n### Key Design Principles\n\n- **Protocol Abstraction**: Codecs (HTTP/1.1, HTTP/2, HTTP/3) are abstracted behind a common interface, allowing HCM to process streams uniformly regardless of protocol.\n- **Lazy Codec Instantiation**: Codecs are created on-demand (H1/H2 on first `onData()`, H3 on `onNewConnection()`), avoiding unnecessary overhead for idle connections.\n- **Streaming Request/Response Processing**: The filter chain processes data as it arrives via callbacks (`decodeHeaders`, `decodeData`, `decodeTrailers`), enabling low-latency proxying.\n- **Filter Chain Iteration Control**: Filters can pause iteration, buffer data, or abort processing, allowing sophisticated request/response manipulation without blocking the event loop.\n\n---\n\n## Component Responsibilities\n\n### 1. ConnectionManagerImpl\n\n**File**: `source/common/http/conn_manager_impl.h/cc`\n\nConnectionManagerImpl is the central bridge between the network layer and HTTP processing. It implements `Network::ReadFilter` and acts as both a connection-level manager and a stream factory.\n\n#### Responsibilities:\n\n**Connection Lifecycle Management**:\n- Implements `Network::ReadFilter::onData()` to receive raw TCP/QUIC bytes\n- Manages connection-level state: idle timelines, max duration, drain decisions\n- Tracks active streams in a doubly-linked list (`streams_`)\n- Signals connection events (close, reset, watermark changes) to all active streams\n\n**Codec Creation and Ownership**:\n- Lazily creates the codec on first `onData()` call (H1/H2) or `onConnection()` (H3)\n- Selects codec based on `codec_type` config or ALPN negotiation\n- Routes incoming data to the codec for stream demultiplexing\n- Handles codec events (stream creation via `newStream()`, protocol errors)\n\n**Stream Lifecycle**:\n- Implements `ServerConnectionCallbacks::newStream()` to create `ActiveStream` objects when the codec receives a new HTTP stream\n- Tracks stream completion and schedules deferred deletion\n- Manages stream-level cleanup: timers, filters, logging\n- Enforces per-connection limits: max requests, request header size, idle timeouts\n\n**Overload and Flow Control**:\n- Integrates with the overload manager to check load shedding points (e.g., `HcmDecodeHeaders`)\n- Manages connection-level write buffer watermarks via `onAboveWriteBufferHighWatermark()` / `onBelowWriteBufferLowWatermark()`\n- Propagates watermark events to the codec and all streams\n\n**Drain State Management**:\n- Decides when to drain connections (max requests reached, graceful shutdown, premature resets detected)\n- Coordinates drain state transitions and sends GOAWAY frames for HTTP/2\n\n**Key State**:\n```cpp\nServerConnectionPtr codec_;        // Protocol codec (H1, H2, or H3)\nstd::list<LinkedObject<ActiveStream>> streams_;  // Active HTTP streams\nDrainState drain_state_;           // Connection drain status\nuint32_t accumulated_requests_;    // Requests processed on this connection\n```\n\n#### Entry Points:\n\n- **`onData(Buffer::Instance&, bool end_stream)`**: Network filter receives downstream bytes \u2192 forwards to codec\n- **`newStream(ResponseEncoder&, bool)`**: Codec signals new HTTP stream \u2192 creates `ActiveStream` and filter chain\n\n---\n\n### 2. FilterManager and HTTP Filter Chain\n\n**Files**: `source/common/http/filter_manager.h/cc`\n\nThe FilterManager is a per-stream filter chain execution engine. It orchestrates the execution of both decoder filters (request path) and encoder filters (response path), managing iteration state, buffering, and local reply generation.\n\n#### Responsibilities:\n\n**Request Processing (Decoder Chain)**:\n- Iterates through decoder filters in order for `decodeHeaders()`, `decodeData()`, `decodeTrailers()`, and `decodeMetadata()`\n- Maintains a `StreamDecoderFilters` collection for forward iteration\n- Stops iteration if a filter returns `StopIteration` or `StopAllIteration`\n- Buffers data if iteration is paused, respecting the stream's buffer limit\n- Calls `onDestroy()` on all filters when the stream completes\n\n**Response Processing (Encoder Chain)**:\n- Iterates through encoder filters in **reverse order** (last filter first)\n- Maintains a `StreamEncoderFilters` collection with reverse iteration\n- Mirrors decoder chain semantics: iteration control, buffering, pause handling\n- Flushes any buffered data when iteration resumes\n\n**Local Reply Generation**:\n- Supports sending local replies (e.g., 404, timeout, authentication failure) without forwarding upstream\n- Can be triggered by filters or HCM (via `FilterManager::sendLocalReply()`)\n- Prepares local replies through all encoder filters to allow header manipulation\n- Properly terminates the decoder chain so no further request processing occurs\n\n**Iteration State Management**:\n- Tracks decode/encode state for each filter: `IterationState::Continue`, `StopIteration`, `StopAllBuffer`, `StopAllWatermark`\n- Buffers data separately if stopped for backpressure (`StopAllWatermark`) vs. custom logic (`StopAllBuffer`)\n- Resumes iteration when a paused filter calls `continueIteration()`\n\n**Watermark and Flow Control**:\n- Manages high/low watermark callbacks for backpressure\n- Calls `onAboveWriteBufferHighWatermark()` / `onBelowWriteBufferLowWatermark()` on subscribed filters\n- Tracks buffered data size and enforces per-stream buffer limits\n\n**Key Abstractions**:\n\n- **`StreamDecoderFilter`**: Implements `decodeHeaders()`, `decodeData()`, `decodeTrailers()`, `decodeMetadata()`\n- **`StreamEncoderFilter`**: Implements `encodeHeaders()`, `encodeData()`, `encodeTrailers()`, `encodeMetadata()`\n- **`StreamFilter`**: Dual filter implementing both decoder and encoder interfaces (e.g., Router filter is a `StreamDecoderFilter`)\n- **`StreamDecoderFilterCallbacks`**: Callbacks for filters to interact with the stream (e.g., `streamInfo()`, `sendLocalReply()`)\n\n#### Filter Chain Creation:\n\nThe FilterManager uses a `FilterChainFactory` (injected at HCM config time) to instantiate filters for each stream:\n\n1. HCM calls `config_->filterFactory().createFilterChain(callbacks)` at stream creation\n2. The factory iterates through configured HTTP filters and instantiates each via a filter config provider\n3. Filters are added to the decoder/encoder chains in registration order\n4. The chain is immutable after creation\n\n#### Key State:\n\n```cpp\nstruct StreamDecoderFilters { std::vector<ActiveStreamDecoderFilterPtr> entries_; };\nstruct StreamEncoderFilters { std::vector<ActiveStreamEncoderFilterPtr> entries_; };\nBuffer::InstancePtr buffered_request_data_;   // Buffered during decoder pause\nBuffer::InstancePtr buffered_response_data_;  // Buffered during encoder pause\nuint64_t buffer_limit_;                       // Max bytes to buffer per stream\n```\n\n---\n\n### 3. Router Filter\n\n**Files**: `source/common/router/router.h/cc`\n\nThe Router filter is the terminal decoder filter in the standard HTTP filter chain. Its primary role is route selection and upstream request forwarding.\n\n#### Responsibilities:\n\n**Route Selection**:\n- Implements `Http::StreamDecoderFilter::decodeHeaders()` to select a route from the configured `RouteConfiguration`\n- Uses `downstreamHeaders()`, stream metadata, and connection context to match against route matchers\n- Selects a cluster name from the matched route's action\n- Caches the selected route in `StreamInfo` for downstream filters and access logs\n\n**Upstream Host Selection**:\n- Queries the cluster manager for a `ThreadLocalCluster` using the route's cluster name\n- Calls the cluster's load balancer to select a specific `Host` endpoint\n- Respects load balancer context from request metadata, cookies, or header-based hash policies\n- Handles load balancer cancellation if host selection takes time or times out\n\n**Upstream Connection Pool Acquisition**:\n- Obtains an HTTP connection pool from the cluster manager for the selected host\n- Passes protocol selection, connection options, and transport socket options\n- Creates a `GenericConnPool` abstraction that works with both HTTP and TCP upstreams\n\n**UpstreamRequest Lifecycle**:\n- Creates an `UpstreamRequest` object for each request to be sent upstream\n- Passes request headers via `acceptHeadersFromRouter()`\n- Passes request data via `acceptDataFromRouter()`\n- Receives upstream response via callbacks on `RouterFilterInterface`\n\n**Retry and Timeout Logic**:\n- Sets up per-try timeouts and global request timeouts\n- Detects retryable upstream failures (connection refused, 503, etc.)\n- Implements exponential backoff and max retry limits\n- Handles hedged requests: spawning parallel upstream requests if `per_try_timeout` is exceeded\n\n**Shadow Routing** (optional):\n- Can spawn shadow requests to a different cluster for testing/canary purposes\n- Shadow requests do not impact the primary response\n- Configured via `RouteEntry::shadowPolicy()`\n\n**Key State**:\n\n```cpp\nstd::list<UpstreamRequestPtr> upstream_requests_;  // Active upstream requests (main + retries + hedges)\nRouter::RouteConstSharedPtr route_;                // Selected route\nUpstream::ClusterInfoConstSharedPtr cluster_;      // Selected cluster\nstd::vector<UpstreamRequest*> pending_hedge_requests_;  // Hedged requests awaiting timeout\n```\n\n#### Filter Interface:\n\n- **`decodeHeaders(RequestHeaderMap&, bool)`**: Select route, host, and create first upstream request\n- **`decodeData(Buffer::Instance&, bool)`**: Forward data to all active upstream requests\n- **`decodeTrailers(RequestTrailerMap&)`**: Forward trailers to upstream\n- **`decodeMetadata(MetadataMap&)`**: Forward metadata to upstream\n- **`onUpstreamHeaders(uint64_t, ResponseHeaderMapPtr&&, UpstreamRequest&, bool)`**: Receive upstream response headers\n- **`onUpstreamData(Buffer::Instance&, UpstreamRequest&, bool)`**: Receive upstream response body\n- **`onUpstreamTrailers(ResponseTrailerMapPtr&&, UpstreamRequest&)`**: Receive upstream response trailers\n\n---\n\n### 4. Cluster Manager and Upstream Connectivity\n\n**Files**: `source/common/upstream/cluster_manager_impl.h/cc`\n\nThe Cluster Manager is Envoy's centralized manager for upstream clusters. It abstracts away cluster membership updates, load balancing, and connection pooling.\n\n#### Responsibilities:\n\n**Cluster Management**:\n- Maintains dynamic cluster configurations via xDS (Cluster Discovery Service)\n- Provides thread-local views of clusters for efficient access without synchronization\n- Implements cluster health checks and outlier detection\n- Notifies listeners of cluster updates (used for graceful connection draining)\n\n**Load Balancer Integration**:\n- Each cluster owns a load balancer (Round Robin, Least Request, Maglev, Random, etc.)\n- The load balancer is queried to select a specific `Host` from the cluster's membership\n- Accepts `LoadBalancerContext` from the router filter containing request metadata, cookies, and headers\n- Implements deterministic selection via consistent hashing and metadata matching\n\n**Connection Pool Management**:\n- Maintains per-host, per-priority, per-protocol connection pools\n- Allocates new pools on-demand and reuses them across requests\n- Manages physical TCP/QUIC connection lifecycle: creation, reuse, closing\n- Implements connection idle detection and draining\n\n**Thread-Local Cluster State**:\n- Stores cluster state in thread-local storage to avoid locks\n- Each worker thread maintains its own set of connection pools\n- Periodically (e.g., on cluster updates) primes thread-local state via callbacks\n\n#### Connection Pool Mechanics:\n\nA connection pool represents a set of physical connections to a single upstream host:\n\n1. **Pool Request**: Router calls `cluster->httpConnPool(host, priority, protocol)` \u2192 returns pool\n2. **Stream Creation**: Router calls `pool->newStream(callbacks)` \u2192 pool either returns existing connection or creates new one\n3. **Connection Ready**: Pool invokes `callbacks->onPoolReady(upstream, ...)` \u2192 UpstreamRequest begins sending data\n4. **Connection Failure**: Pool invokes `callbacks->onPoolFailure(reason)` \u2192 router triggers retry logic\n\n#### Key Abstractions:\n\n- **`Cluster`**: Represents a named group of upstream endpoints; owns load balancer and config\n- **`Host`**: An individual upstream endpoint with address, health status, and metadata\n- **`ClusterManager`**: Factory for getting thread-local views of clusters\n- **`ThreadLocalCluster`**: Per-worker-thread view; provides `chooseHost()` and `httpConnPool()`\n- **`ConnectionPool::Instance`**: Manages connections to a single host; spawns new streams on available connections\n\n#### Load Balancing:\n\n1. Router calls `cluster->loadBalancer()->chooseHost(context)` to select a host\n2. Load balancer uses context's hash key, metadata, or direct host assignment\n3. Returns a host or nullptr if all hosts are unhealthy\n4. Router then queries the connection pool for that host\n\n---\n\n## Data Flow\n\n### Request Path (Downstream to Upstream)\n\n```\nDownstream TCP/QUIC bytes\n    \u2193\nConnectionManagerImpl::onData()\n    \u2193\n[Create codec if needed (H1/H2 on first data, H3 on connection)]\n    \u2193\nCodec demultiplexes stream from bytes\n    \u2193\nCodec::ServerConnectionCallbacks::newStream(response_encoder, stream_id)\n    \u2193\nConnectionManagerImpl::newStream()\n    \u251c\u2500 Create ActiveStream\n    \u251c\u2500 Create buffer account for watermark tracking\n    \u251c\u2500 Create FilterManager\n    \u251c\u2500 Call filterFactory_.createFilterChain(callbacks)\n    \u2502   \u2514\u2500 Instantiate all configured HTTP filters\n    \u2514\u2500 Return RequestDecoder to codec\n    \u2193\nCodec calls RequestDecoder::decodeHeaders(headers, end_stream)\n    \u2193\nConnectionManagerImpl::ActiveStream::decodeHeaders()\n    \u251c\u2500 Pass headers to FilterManager\n    \u2514\u2500 FilterManager::decodeHeaders(headers, end_stream)\n        \u251c\u2500 Iterate decoder filters in order\n        \u251c\u2500 Call filter1->decodeHeaders(), filter2->decodeHeaders(), ..., routerFilter->decodeHeaders()\n        \u251c\u2500 Router filter selects route and creates upstream request(s)\n        \u2514\u2500 Each filter returns FilterHeadersStatus:\n           - Continue \u2192 next filter\n           - StopIteration \u2192 buffer data, wait for continueIteration()\n           - StopAllIteration \u2192 buffer all data, don't call further filters\n    \u2193\n[Router filter creates UpstreamRequest and acquires connection pool]\n    \u2193\nUpstreamRequest::acceptHeadersFromRouter(end_stream)\n    \u251c\u2500 Pass headers to UpstreamFilterManager\n    \u2514\u2500 Iterate upstream HTTP filters (if configured)\n        \u2514\u2500 Call codec filter to encode headers\n    \u2193\n[Upstream connection established or reused from pool]\n    \u2193\nCodec::newStream() \u2192 RequestEncoder\n    \u2193\nRequestEncoder encodes request headers to upstream connection\n    \u2193\nCodec calls RequestDecoder::decodeData(data, end_stream) [if body present]\n    \u2193\nConnectionManagerImpl::ActiveStream::decodeData()\n    \u2514\u2500 FilterManager::decodeData(data, end_stream)\n        \u2514\u2500 Iterate decoder filters, forward data to router\n    \u2193\nUpstreamRequest::acceptDataFromRouter(data, end_stream)\n    \u2514\u2500 Iterate upstream filters, encode to RequestEncoder\n    \u2193\nRequestEncoder writes data to upstream connection buffer\n    \u2193\n[Repeat for trailers and metadata if present]\n```\n\n### Response Path (Upstream to Downstream)\n\n```\nUpstream bytes arrive on connection\n    \u2193\nCodec decodes upstream response\n    \u2193\nResponseDecoder callbacks fired (e.g., decodeHeaders, decodeData, decodeTrailers)\n    \u2193\nUpstreamRequest::decodeHeaders(headers, end_stream) [response headers]\n    \u251c\u2500 Pass headers through UpstreamFilterManager (filters in reverse order)\n    \u2514\u2500 Call RouterFilterInterface::onUpstreamHeaders(status, headers, upstream_request, end_stream)\n    \u2193\nRouter::onUpstreamHeaders()\n    \u251c\u2500 Store response headers in stream\n    \u2514\u2500 Call FilterManager::encodeHeaders(headers, end_stream)\n        \u251c\u2500 Iterate encoder filters in reverse order\n        \u251c\u2500 Call routerFilter->encodeHeaders(), filter2->encodeHeaders(), ..., filter1->encodeHeaders()\n        \u2514\u2500 Each filter returns FilterHeadersStatus:\n           - Continue \u2192 next filter\n           - StopIteration \u2192 buffer data, wait for continueIteration()\n    \u2193\n[Encoder filters can modify response headers (add authentication, rewrite location, etc.)]\n    \u2193\nLast encoder filter (or early encoder if no filters) calls ResponseEncoder::encodeHeaders()\n    \u2193\nDownstream codec encodes headers to client connection\n    \u2193\n[Response body and trailers follow same path through encoder filters]\n    \u2193\nBytes sent to downstream client\n```\n\n### Stream Completion\n\n```\nEither upstream sends end_stream or decoder filter aborts:\n    \u2193\nFilterManager::maybeEndDecode(terminal_filter_end_stream)\n    \u251c\u2500 Marks decoder chain as complete\n    \u251c\u2500 Stops accepting further request data\n    \u2514\u2500 If encoder already complete \u2192 checkAndCloseStream()\n    \u2193\nFilterManager::maybeEndEncode(end_stream)\n    \u251c\u2500 Marks encoder chain as complete\n    \u251c\u2500 Stops accepting further response data\n    \u2514\u2500 If decoder already complete \u2192 checkAndCloseStream()\n    \u2193\nFilterManager::checkAndCloseStream()\n    \u251c\u2500 Call filter->onStreamComplete() for all filters\n    \u251c\u2500 Destroy filters\n    \u2514\u2500 Return stream to ConnectionManagerImpl\n    \u2193\nConnectionManagerImpl::doDeferredStreamDestroy()\n    \u251c\u2500 Log access logs\n    \u251c\u2500 Disable timers\n    \u251c\u2500 Reset stream if needed (e.g., for protocol errors)\n    \u2514\u2500 Schedule stream deletion via dispatcher.deferredDelete()\n    \u2193\nStream memory freed; connection ready for next stream\n```\n\n---\n\n## Extension Points\n\nEnvoy's HTTP request processing is highly extensible through several well-defined extension mechanisms:\n\n### 1. HTTP Filters\n\n**Interface**: `StreamDecoderFilter`, `StreamEncoderFilter`, `StreamFilter`\n\nHTTP filters are the primary extension point. Custom filters can:\n- Inspect and modify request/response headers, body, trailers\n- Implement authentication, authorization, rate limiting, load shedding\n- Perform request/response body transformation (compression, encryption)\n- Generate local replies (short-circuit requests)\n- Control filter iteration (pause, resume, abort)\n\n**Example**: The built-in router filter is itself an HTTP filter implementing `StreamDecoderFilter`.\n\n**Registration**: Filters are registered in the HTTP connection manager config:\n```yaml\nhttp_filters:\n  - name: envoy.filters.http.auth\n    typed_config: { ... }\n  - name: envoy.filters.http.lua\n    typed_config: { ... }\n  - name: envoy.filters.http.router  # Always last\n    typed_config: { ... }\n```\n\nFilters are instantiated via a `FilterChainFactory` that is passed to each `FilterManager`.\n\n### 2. Route Configuration and Cluster Selection\n\n**Interface**: `RouteConfiguration`, `RouteEntry`, `Route`\n\nRoutes define how requests are matched and forwarded:\n- **Matchers**: Path prefix/exact/regex, headers, methods, query parameters\n- **Actions**: Forward to cluster, redirect, direct response, circuit breaking rules\n- **Request Transformation**: Add/remove headers, request ID generation\n- **Retry Policy**: Max retries, retryable status codes, backoff strategy\n- **Timeout**: Request timeout, per-try timeout\n- **Mirror/Shadow**: Route a copy of the request to another cluster\n\nRoutes can be:\n- Statically configured in the bootstrap config\n- Dynamically updated via RDS (Route Discovery Service)\n- Scoped to specific criteria (virtual hosts, per-node configuration)\n\n### 3. Load Balancing\n\n**Interface**: `LoadBalancer`, `LoadBalancerContext`\n\nCluster managers use pluggable load balancers:\n- **Round Robin**: Distribute evenly across healthy hosts\n- **Least Request**: Route to host with fewest active requests\n- **Maglev**: Consistent hashing with deterministic subset selection\n- **Random**: Random host selection\n- **Original Destination**: Route to upstream's original destination IP\n\nCustom load balancers can implement sophisticated algorithms (e.g., per-cookie session affinity, ML-based routing).\n\nLoad balancers receive `LoadBalancerContext` from the router:\n```cpp\nstruct LoadBalancerContext {\n  absl::optional<uint64_t> hash_key;           // Consistent hash\n  const Protobuf::Struct* connection_metadata; // Dynamic metadata\n  const Protobuf::Struct* request_metadata;    // Request-specific metadata\n};\n```\n\n### 4. Upstream Connection Pools\n\n**Interface**: `ConnectionPool::InstancePtr`\n\nConnection pool factories are provided by cluster managers, allowing:\n- Custom connection pooling strategies (connection limits, idle detection)\n- Protocol negotiation (ALPN for HTTP/1.1 vs. HTTP/2)\n- Connection reuse policies (keep-alive, max requests per connection)\n\n### 5. Access Logging\n\n**Interface**: `AccessLog::InstanceSharedPtr`\n\nAccess loggers receive complete `StreamInfo` containing:\n- Request/response headers, trailers\n- Upstream cluster and host\n- Duration and timing information\n- Response flags (error conditions, retry counts)\n- Custom filter state\n\nLoggers can format and emit logs to:\n- Local file (gRPC, JSON, plaintext)\n- Remote syslog server\n- gRPC service\n- Custom backend via extension\n\n### 6. Request ID Generation\n\n**Interface**: `RequestIDExtension`\n\nCustom request ID generators can:\n- Generate request IDs based on request properties\n- Set request IDs in custom headers\n- Trace requests across distributed systems\n\n### 7. Custom Filter State\n\n**Interface**: `StreamInfo::FilterState`\n\nFilters can store arbitrary per-request or per-connection state:\n```cpp\nstream_info.filterState()->setData<MyCustomObject>(\n    \"my.custom.key\",\n    std::make_unique<MyCustomObject>(),\n    StreamInfo::FilterState::StateType::Mutable\n);\n```\n\nDownstream filters can retrieve this state and act on it.\n\n### 8. Tracing\n\n**Interface**: `Tracer`, `Span`\n\nTracers integrate with Envoy's request processing:\n- Receive span creation callbacks at critical points\n- Inject trace context into upstream request headers (via `x-b3-trace-id`, `traceparent`, etc.)\n- Extract trace context from downstream headers\n- Report spans to tracing backends (Jaeger, Zipkin, Datadog, AWS X-Ray)\n\n### 9. Stats and Metrics\n\n**Interface**: `Stats::Scope`, `Stats::Statistic`\n\nFilters and cluster managers emit rich metrics:\n- Request counts, errors, latencies\n- Upstream health status and failover events\n- Connection pooling statistics\n- Custom filter-specific metrics\n\n---\n\n## Error Handling\n\nEnvoy handles errors at multiple layers with graceful degradation:\n\n### Codec Errors (H1, H2, H3)\n\n**Detection**: Codec detects malformed headers, invalid frames, protocol violations\n\n**Handling**:\n- Codec sets `StreamInfo::DownstreamProtocolError` flag\n- Sends HTTP 400 Bad Request to client (if stream is viable)\n- If protocol is unrecoverable: closes connection with GOAWAY (H2) or connection reset (H1)\n- Logs error for debugging\n\n**Example**: Invalid HTTP/2 frame size \u2192 codec error \u2192 400 response \u2192 connection reused if possible\n\n### Filter Errors\n\n**Detection**: Filter calls `sendLocalReply()` or logs an error; filter returns `StopIteration`\n\n**Handling**:\n- FilterManager stops decoder chain execution\n- FilterManager calls `sendLocalReply()` to generate HTTP response\n- Response headers pass through remaining encoder filters\n- Stream completes normally with error response\n\n**Example**: Authentication filter denies request \u2192 `sendLocalReply(401)` \u2192 401 returned to client\n\n### Upstream Connection Failures\n\n**Detection**: Connection pool fails to connect, connection drops, or TLS handshake fails\n\n**Handling**:\n1. Pool invokes `GenericConnectionPoolCallbacks::onPoolFailure(PoolFailureReason, host)`\n2. UpstreamRequest invokes `RouterFilterInterface::onUpstreamReset(StreamResetReason)`\n3. Router checks route's retry policy:\n   - If retryable and retries remaining: create new UpstreamRequest\n   - If non-retryable or retries exhausted: send upstream error response (503, 504, etc.)\n4. Response flows back through encoder filters\n5. Stream completes with error response\n\n**Retry Backoff**: Router implements exponential backoff (jitter optional) between retries\n\n**Response Flags**: Router sets response flags in `StreamInfo` (e.g., `UpstreamConnectionFailure`, `UpstreamRequestTimeout`)\n\n### Timeout Errors\n\n**Request Timeout** (global deadline for entire request):\n- Triggered by timer if request exceeds `timeout` configured on route\n- FilterManager calls `sendLocalReply(504 Gateway Timeout)`\n- Router cancels any pending upstream requests\n\n**Per-Try Timeout** (deadline for each retry attempt):\n- Triggered by timer if individual try exceeds `per_try_timeout`\n- Router triggers retry if retries remaining\n- Enables hedged requests: if timeout expires before response, spawn parallel request\n\n**Idle Timeout** (connection-level):\n- ConnectionManagerImpl closes idle connections after `idle_timeout`\n- Prevents connection leaks if clients are hung\n\n### Upstream Protocol Errors\n\n**Detection**: Upstream sends invalid response headers, body framing errors, etc.\n\n**Handling**:\n- ResponseDecoder sets `StreamInfo::UpstreamProtocolError` flag\n- If possible, stream continues with best-effort parsing\n- Otherwise, router triggers reset and sends error response\n\n### Resource Exhaustion\n\n**High Watermark** (downstream buffer full):\n- FilterManager detects buffered data exceeds limit\n- Calls `onAboveWriteBufferHighWatermark()` on watermark subscribers (typically router)\n- Router stops reading from downstream connection (backpressure)\n- Once buffer drained: `onBelowWriteBufferLowWatermark()` resumes reading\n\n**Overload Shedding**:\n- ConnectionManagerImpl checks overload points before accepting new streams\n- If overload shed point is active: sends 503 Service Unavailable without filter processing\n- Prevents cascading failures during sustained overload\n\n---\n\n## Relevant Source Files\n\n### Core Components\n\n| Component | Header | instantiation\n2. **Per-stream Processing** \u2192 **FilterManager** \u2192 Ordered filter chain iteration\n3. **Route Selection & Forwarding** \u2192 **Router Filter** \u2192 Upstream acquisition\n4.    // Requests processed on this connection\n```\n\n#### Entry Points:\n\n- **`onData(Buffer::Instance&, bool end_stream)`**: Network filter receives downstream bytes \u2192 forwards to codec\n- **`newStream(ResponseEncoder&, bool)`**: Codec signals new HTTP stream \u2192 creates `ActiveStream` and filter chain\n\n---\n\n### 2. It orchestrates the execution of both decoder filters (request path) and encoder filters (response path), managing iteration state, buffering, and local reply generation.\n\n#### Responsibilities:\n\n**Request Processing (Decoder Chain)**:\n- Iterates through decoder filters in order for `decodeHeaders()`, `decodeData()`, `decodeTrailers()`, and `decodeMetadata()`\n- Maintains a `StreamDecoderFilters` collection for forward iteration\n- Stops iteration if a filter returns `StopIteration` or `StopAllIteration`\n- Buffers data if iteration is paused, respecting the stream's buffer limit\n- Calls `onDestroy()` on all filters when the stream completes\n\n**Response Processing (Encoder Chain)**:\n- Iterates through encoder filters in **reverse order** (last filter first)\n- Maintains a `StreamEncoderFilters` collection with reverse iteration\n- Mirrors decoder chain semantics: iteration control, buffering, pause handling\n- Flushes any buffered data when iteration resumes\n\n**Local Reply Generation**:\n- Supports sending local replies (e.g., 404, timeout, authentication failure) without forwarding upstream\n- Can be triggered by filters or HCM (via `FilterManager::sendLocalReply()`)\n- Prepares local replies through all encoder filters to allow header manipulation\n- Properly terminates the decoder chain so no further request processing occurs",

# Envoy HTTP Connection Manager Architecture

## Overview

The HTTP Connection Manager (HCM) is Envoy's core subsystem for processing HTTP requests from downstream clients through to upstream servers. It acts as a **network-level filter** that owns the full lifecycle of downstream TCP/QUIC connections, creating and managing per-stream HTTP processing pipelines.

The HCM architecture centers on four primary components working together:

1. **ConnectionManagerImpl** — Connection lifecycle manager and codec orchestrator
2. **FilterManager and HTTP Filter Chain** — Per-stream request/response processing engine
3. **Router Filter** — Terminal decoder filter that performs route selection and upstream dispatch
4. **Cluster Manager and Upstream Connectivity** — Upstream connection pooling and load balancing

### Key Design Principles

- **Protocol Abstraction**: Codecs (HTTP/1.1, HTTP/2, HTTP/3) are abstracted behind a common interface, allowing HCM to process streams uniformly regardless of protocol.
- **Lazy Codec Instantiation**: Codecs are created on-demand (H1/H2 on first `onData()`, H3 on `onNewConnection()`), avoiding unnecessary overhead for idle connections.
- **Streaming Request/Response Processing**: The filter chain processes data as it arrives via callbacks (`decodeHeaders`, `decodeData`, `decodeTrailers`), enabling low-latency proxying.
- **Filter Chain Iteration Control**: Filters can pause iteration, buffer data, or abort processing, allowing sophisticated request/response manipulation without blocking the event loop.

---

## Component Responsibilities

### 1. ConnectionManagerImpl

**File**: `source/common/http/conn_manager_impl.h/cc`

ConnectionManagerImpl is the central bridge between the network layer and HTTP processing. It implements `Network::ReadFilter`
